0004b068                 bool is_non_triangular_conic_curve() {

0004b2b3             float2 p0=p01.xy, p1=p01.zw, p2=p23.xy, p3=p23.zw;
0004b2f2             if (is_conic_curve()) {
0004b316                 // Conics are 3 points, with the weight in p3.
0004b355                 float w = p3.x;
0004b375                 p3 = p2;  // Duplicate the endpoint for shared code that also runs on cubics.
0004b3d3                 if (is_non_triangular_conic_curve()) {
0004b40a                     // Convert the points to a trapeziodal hull that circumcscribes the conic.
0004b469                     float2 p1w = p1 * w;
0004b492                     float T = .51;  // Bias outward a bit to ensure we cover the outermost samples.
0004b4f6                     float2 c1 = mix(p0, p1w, T);
0004b527                     float2 c2 = mix(p2, p1w, T);
0004b558                     float iw = 1 / mix(1, w, T);
0004b589                     p2 = c2 * iw;
0004b5ab                     p1 = c1 * iw;
0004b5cd                 }
0004b5df             }
0004b5ee             // Translate the points to v0..3 where v0=0.
0004b627             float2 v1 = p1 - p0;
0004b648             float2 v2 = p2 - p0;
0004b669             float2 v3 = p3 - p0;
0004b68b             // Reorder the points so v2 bisects v1 and v3.
0004b6c6             if (sign(cross_length_2d(v2, v1)) == sign(cross_length_2d(v2, v3))) {
0004b718                 float2 tmp = p2;
0004b739                 if (sign(cross_length_2d(v1, v2)) != sign(cross_length_2d(v1, v3))) {
0004b78f                     p2 = p1;  // swap(p2, p1)
0004b7bd                     p1 = tmp;
0004b7db                 } else {
0004b7f4                     p2 = p3;  // swap(p2, p3)
0004b822                     p3 = tmp;
0004b840                 }
0004b852             }
0004b861             // Negative argsAttr.z means the join is an internal chop or circle, and both of
0004b8be             // those have empty joins. All we need is a bevel join.
0004b902             if (argsAttr.z < 0) {
0004b924                 // +2 because we emit the beginning and ending edges twice (see above comment).
0004b984                 numEdgesInJoin = 1 + 2;
0004b9ac             }
0004b9bb             if (JOIN_TYPE >= 0 /*Is the join not a round type?*/) {
0004b9ff                 // Bevel and miter joins get 1 and 2 segments respectively.
0004ba4b                 // +2 because we emit the beginning and ending edges twice (see above comments).
0004baac                 numEdgesInJoin = sign(JOIN_TYPE) + 1 + 2;
0004bae6             }

0004bbb8             void main() {
0004bbd2                 mat4x2 P = mat4x2(vsPt[0], vsPt[1], vsPt[2], vsPt[3]);
0004bc19                 float numSegments;
0004bc3c                 if (isinf(P[3].y)) {
0004bc61                     // This is a conic.
0004bc89                     float w = P[3].x;
0004bcaf                     numSegments = wangs_formula_conic(PRECISION, P[0], P[1], P[2], w);
0004bd06                     // Convert to a rational cubic in projected form.
0004bd4c                     rationalCubicXY = mat4x2(P[0],
0004bd7f                                              mix(vec4(P[0], P[2]), (P[1] * w).xyxy, 2.0/3.0),
0004bddd                                              P[2]);
0004be11                     rationalCubicW = fma(w, 2.0/3.0, 1.0/3.0);
0004be50                 } else {
0004be69                     // This is a cubic.
0004be91                     numSegments = wangs_formula_cubic(PRECISION, P[0], P[1], P[2], P[3], mat2(1));
0004bef4                     rationalCubicXY = P;
0004bf1d                     rationalCubicW = 1;
0004bf45                 }
0004bf57                 fanpoint = vsPt[4];
0004bf7c                 // Tessellate the first side of the patch into numSegments triangles.
0004bfd2                 gl_TessLevelOuter[0] = min(numSegments, MAX_TESSELLATION_SEGMENTS);
0004c027                 // Leave the other two sides of the patch as single segments.
0004c075                 gl_TessLevelOuter[1] = 1.0;
0004c0a1                 gl_TessLevelOuter[2] = 1.0;
0004c0ce                 // Changing the inner level to 1 when numSegments == 1 collapses the entire
0004c12a                 // patch to a single triangle. Otherwise, we need an inner level of 2 so our curve
0004c18d                 // triangles have an interior point to originate from.
0004c1d4                 gl_TessLevelInner[0] = min(numSegments, 2.0);

0004c221             layout(vertices = 1) out;
0004c248             in vec2 P[];
0004c261             patch out mat4x2 rationalCubicXY;
0004c28f             patch out float rationalCubicW;
0004c2bc             void main() {
0004c2d6                 float w = -1;  // w<0 means a cubic.
0004c30b                 vec2 p1w = P[1];
0004c32c                 if (isinf(P[3].y)) {
0004c351                     // This patch is actually a conic. Project to homogeneous space.
0004c3a6                     w = P[3].x;
0004c3c6                     p1w *= w;
0004c3e4                 }
0004c3f7                 // Chop the curve at T=1/2.
0004c423                 vec2 ab = (P[0] + p1w) * .5;
0004c450                 vec2 bc = (p1w + P[2]) * .5;
0004c47d                 vec2 cd = (P[2] + P[3]) * .5;
0004c4ab                 vec2 abc = (ab + bc) * .5;
0004c4d6                 vec2 bcd = (bc + cd) * .5;
0004c501                 vec2 abcd = (abc + bcd) * .5;
0004c530                 float n0, n1;
0004c54e                 if (w < 0 || isinf(w)) {
0004c577                     if (w < 0) {
0004c598                         // The patch is a cubic. Calculate how many segments are required to
0004c5f5                         // linearize each half of the curve.
0004c632                         n0 = wangs_formula_cubic(PRECISION, P[0], ab, abc, abcd, mat2(1));
0004c68d                         n1 = wangs_formula_cubic(PRECISION, abcd, bcd, cd, P[3], mat2(1));
0004c6e8                         rationalCubicW = 1;
0004c714                     } else {
0004c731                         // The patch is a triangle (a conic with infinite weight).
0004c784                         n0 = n1 = 1;
0004c7a9                         rationalCubicW = -1;  // In the next stage, rationalCubicW<0 means triangle.
0004c80e                     }
0004c824                     rationalCubicXY = mat4x2(P[0], P[1], P[2], P[3]);
0004c86a                 } else {
0004c883                     // The patch is a conic. Unproject p0..5. w1 == w2 == w3 when chopping at .5.
0004c8e5                     // (See SkConic::chopAt().)
0004c915                     float r = 2.0 / (1.0 + w);
0004c944                     ab *= r, bc *= r, abc *= r;
0004c974                     // Put in "standard form" where w0 == w2 == w4 == 1.
0004c9bd                     float w_ = inversesqrt(r);  // Both halves have the same w' when chopping at .5.
0004ca22                     // Calculate how many segments are needed to linearize each half of the curve.
0004ca85                     n0 = wangs_formula_conic(PRECISION, P[0], ab, abc, w_);
0004cad1                     n1 = wangs_formula_conic(PRECISION, abc, bc, P[2], w_);
0004cb1d                     // Covert the conic to a rational cubic in projected form.
0004cb6c                     rationalCubicXY = mat4x2(P[0],
0004cb9f                                              mix(float4(P[0],P[2]), p1w.xyxy, 2.0/3.0),
0004cbf7                                              P[2]);
0004cc2b                     rationalCubicW = fma(w, 2.0/3.0, 1.0/3.0);
0004cc6a                 }
0004cc7d                 gl_TessLevelOuter[0] = min(n1, MAX_TESSELLATION_SEGMENTS);
0004ccc8                 gl_TessLevelOuter[1] = 1.0;
0004ccf4                 gl_TessLevelOuter[2] = min(n0, MAX_TESSELLATION_SEGMENTS);
0004cd40                 // Changing the inner level to 1 when n0 == n1 == 1 collapses the entire patch to a
0004cda4                 // single triangle. Otherwise, we need an inner level of 2 so our curve triangles
0004ce06                 // have an interior point to originate from.
0004ce43                 gl_TessLevelInner[0] = min(max(n0, n1), 2.0);
0004ce81             }

0004cf47             void main() {
0004cf61                 vec2 vertexpos;
0004cf81                 if (rationalCubicW < 0) {  // rationalCubicW < 0 means a triangle now.
0004cfd8                     vertexpos = (gl_TessCoord.x != 0) ? rationalCubicXY[0]
0004d023                               : (gl_TessCoord.y != 0) ? rationalCubicXY[1]
0004d06e                                                       : rationalCubicXY[2];
0004d0ba                 } else {
0004d0d3                     // Locate our parametric point of interest. T ramps from [0..1/2] on the left
0004d135                     // edge of the triangle, and [1/2..1] on the right. If we are the patch's
0004d193                     // interior vertex, then we want T=1/2. Since the barycentric coords are
0004d1f0                     // (1/3, 1/3, 1/3) at the interior vertex, the below fma() works in all 3
0004d24e                     // scenarios.
0004d270                     float T = fma(.5, gl_TessCoord.y, gl_TessCoord.z);
0004d2b8                     mat4x3 P = mat4x3(rationalCubicXY[0], 1,
0004d2f5                                       rationalCubicXY[1], rationalCubicW,
0004d33f                                       rationalCubicXY[2], rationalCubicW,
0004d389                                       rationalCubicXY[3], 1);
0004d3c7                     vertexpos = eval_rational_cubic(P, T);
0004d402                     if (all(notEqual(gl_TessCoord.xz, vec2(0)))) {
0004d445                         // We are the interior point of the patch; center it inside
0004d499                         // [C(0), C(.5), C(1)].
0004d4c9                         vertexpos = (P[0].xy + vertexpos + P[3].xy) / 3.0;
0004d514                     }
0004d52a                 }
0004d53d                 gl_Position = vec4(vertexpos * sk_RTAdjust.xz + sk_RTAdjust.yw, 0.0, 1.0);

0004d682             void main() {
0004d69c                 // Locate our parametric point of interest. It is equal to the barycentric
0004d6f7                 // y-coordinate if we are a vertex on the tessellated edge of the triangle patch,
0004d759                 // 0.5 if we are the patch's interior vertex, or N/A if we are the fan point.
0004d7b7                 // NOTE: We are on the tessellated edge when the barycentric x-coordinate == 0.
0004d817                 float T = (gl_TessCoord.x == 0.0) ? gl_TessCoord.y : 0.5;
0004d862                 mat4x3 P = mat4x3(rationalCubicXY[0], 1,
0004d89b                                   rationalCubicXY[1], rationalCubicW,
0004d8e1                                   rationalCubicXY[2], rationalCubicW,
0004d927                                   rationalCubicXY[3], 1);
0004d961                 vec2 vertexpos = eval_rational_cubic(P, T);
0004d99e                 if (gl_TessCoord.x == 1.0) {
0004d9cb                     // We are the anchor point that fans from the center of the curve's contour.
0004da2c                     vertexpos = fanpoint;
0004da56                 } else if (gl_TessCoord.x != 0.0) {
0004da8a                     // We are the interior point of the patch; center it inside [C(0), C(.5), C(1)].
0004daef                     vertexpos = (P[0].xy + vertexpos + P[3].xy) / 3.0;
0004db36                 }
0004db49                 gl_Position = vec4(vertexpos * sk_RTAdjust.xz + sk_RTAdjust.yw, 0.0, 1.0);
0004dba4             }

0004dced     void main() {
0004dcff         // Our patch is composed of exactly "numTotalCombinedSegments + 1" stroke-width edges that
0004dd62         // run orthogonal to the curve and make a strip of "numTotalCombinedSegments" quads.
0004ddbf         // Determine which discrete edge belongs to this invocation. An edge can either come from a
0004de23         // parametric segment or a radial one.
0004de52         float numSegmentsInJoin = tcsJoinArgs0.x;
0004de84         float numTotalCombinedSegments = numSegmentsInJoin + tcsTessArgs[0].x + tcsTessArgs[1].x +
0004dee7                                          tcsTessArgs[2].x;
0004df22         float combinedEdgeID = round(gl_TessCoord.x * numTotalCombinedSegments);
0004df73         float strokeOutset = gl_TessCoord.y * 2.0 - 1.0;
0004dfad         // Furthermore, the vertex shader may have chopped the curve into 3 different sections.
0004e00d         // Determine which section we belong to, and where we fall relative to its first edge.
0004e06c         float2 p0, p1, p2, p3;
0004e08b         vec2 tan0;
0004e09e         float numParametricSegments, radsPerSegment;
0004e0d3         if (combinedEdgeID < numSegmentsInJoin || numSegmentsInJoin == numTotalCombinedSegments) {
0004e136             // Our edge belongs to the join preceding the curve.
0004e177             p3 = p2 = p1 = p0 = tcsPts01[0].xy;
0004e1a7             tan0 = tcsJoinArgs0.zw;
0004e1cb             numParametricSegments = 1;
0004e1f2             radsPerSegment = tcsJoinArgs1.x;
0004e21f             strokeOutset = clamp(strokeOutset, tcsJoinArgs1.y, tcsJoinArgs1.z);
0004e26f             strokeOutset *= (combinedEdgeID == 1.0) ? tcsJoinArgs0.y : 1.0;
0004e2bb         } else if ((combinedEdgeID -= numSegmentsInJoin) < tcsTessArgs[0].x) {
0004e30a             // Our edge belongs to the first curve section.
0004e346             p0=tcsPts01[0].xy, p1=tcsPts01[0].zw, p2=tcsPt2Tan0[0].xy, p3=tcsPts01[1].xy;
0004e3a0             tan0 = tcsPt2Tan0[0].zw;
0004e3c5             numParametricSegments = tcsTessArgs[0].y;
0004e3fb             radsPerSegment = tcsTessArgs[0].z;
0004e42a         } else if ((combinedEdgeID -= tcsTessArgs[0].x) < tcsTessArgs[1].x) {
0004e478             // Our edge belongs to the second curve section.
0004e4b5             p0=tcsPts01[1].xy, p1=tcsPts01[1].zw, p2=tcsPt2Tan0[1].xy, p3=tcsPts01[2].xy;
0004e50f             tan0 = tcsPt2Tan0[1].zw;
0004e534             numParametricSegments = tcsTessArgs[1].y;
0004e56a             radsPerSegment = tcsTessArgs[1].z;
0004e599         } else {
0004e5aa             // Our edge belongs to the third curve section.
0004e5e6             combinedEdgeID -= tcsTessArgs[1].x;
0004e616             p0=tcsPts01[2].xy, p1=tcsPts01[2].zw, p2=tcsPt2Tan0[2].xy, p3=tcsEndPtEndTan.xy;
0004e673             tan0 = tcsPt2Tan0[2].zw;
0004e698             numParametricSegments = tcsTessArgs[2].y;
0004e6ce             radsPerSegment = tcsTessArgs[2].z;
0004e6fd         }
0004e707         float2 tan1 = tcsEndPtEndTan.zw;
0004e730         bool isFinalEdge = (gl_TessCoord.x == 1);
0004e762         float w = -1.0;  // w<0 means the curve is an integral cubic.
0004e7a8         if (isinf(p3.y)) {
0004e7c3             w = p3.x;  // The curve is actually a conic.
0004e7fc             p3 = p2;  // Setting p3 equal to p2 works for the remaining rotational logic.
0004e856         }
0004e861         // Unpack the curve args from the vertex shader.
0004e89a         mat4x2 P;
0004e8ac         mat2 tangents;
0004e8c3         if (gl_InvocationID == 0) {
0004e8e7             // This is the first section of the curve.
0004e91e             P = mat4x2(vsPts01[0], vsPts23[0]);
0004e94e             tangents = mat2(vsTans01[0]);
0004e978         } else if (gl_InvocationID == 1) {
0004e9a3             // This is the middle section of the curve.
0004e9db             P = mat4x2(vsPts23[0].zw, vsPts45[0], vsPts67[0].xy);
0004ea1d             tangents = mat2(vsTans01[0].zw, vsTans23[0].xy);
0004ea5a         } else {
0004ea6b             // This is the final section of the curve.
0004eaa2             P = mat4x2(vsPts67[0], vsPts89[0]);
0004ead2             tangents = mat2(vsTans23[0]);
0004eafc         }
0004eb07         // Calculate the number of parametric segments. The final tessellated strip will be a
0004eb65         // composition of these parametric segments as well as radial segments.
0004ebb5         float w = isinf(P[3].y) ? P[3].x : -1.0; // w<0 means the curve is an integral cubic.
0004ec13         float numParametricSegments;
0004ec38         if (w < 0.0) {
0004ec4f             numParametricSegments = wangs_formula_cubic(MAX_SCALE * PRECISION, P[0], P[1], P[2],
0004ecb0                                                         P[3], mat2(1));
0004ecf8         } else {
0004ed09             numParametricSegments = wangs_formula_conic(MAX_SCALE * PRECISION, P[0], P[1], P[2], w);
0004ed6e         }
0004ed78         if (P[0] == P[1] && P[2] == P[3]) {
0004eda4             // This is how the patch builder articulates lineTos but Wang's formula returns
0004ee00             // >>1 segment in this scenario. Assign 1 parametric segment.
0004ee4a             numParametricSegments = 1.0;
0004ee73         }
0004ee7e         // Determine the curve's total rotation. The vertex shader ensures our curve does not rotate
0004eee3         // more than 180 degrees or inflect, so the inverse cosine has enough range.
0004ef38         float cosTheta = cosine_between_vectors(tangents[0], tangents[1]);
0004ef83         float rotation = acos(cosTheta);
0004efad         // Adjust sign of rotation to match the direction the curve turns.
0004eff8         // NOTE: Since the curve is not allowed to inflect, we can just check F'(.5) x F''(.5).
0004f058         // NOTE: F'(.5) x F''(.5) has the same sign as (P2 - P0) x (P3 - P1)
0004f0a5         float turn = isinf(P[3].y) ? cross2d(P[1] - P[0], P[2] - P[1])
0004f0ec                                    : cross2d(P[2] - P[0], P[3] - P[1]);
0004f134         if (turn == 0.0) {  // This is the case for joins and cusps where points are co-located.
0004f195             turn = determinant(tangents);
0004f1bf         }
0004f1c9         if (turn < 0.0) {
0004f1e3             rotation = -rotation;
0004f205         }
0004f210         // Calculate the number of evenly spaced radial segments to chop this section of the curve
0004f273         // into. Radial segments divide the curve's rotation into even steps. The final tessellated
0004f2d7         // strip will be a composition of both parametric and radial segments.
0004f326         float numRadialSegments = abs(rotation) * NUM_RADIAL_SEGMENTS_PER_RADIAN;
0004f378         numRadialSegments = max(ceil(numRadialSegments), 1.0);
0004f3b8         // The first and last edges are shared by both the parametric and radial sets of edges, so
0004f41b         // the total number of edges is:
0004f444         //
0004f44f         //   numCombinedEdges = numParametricEdges + numRadialEdges - 2
0004f497         //
0004f4a2         // It's also important to differentiate between the number of edges and segments in a strip:
0004f507         //
0004f512         //   numCombinedSegments = numCombinedEdges - 1
0004f54a         //
0004f555         // So the total number of segments in the combined strip is:
0004f59a         //
0004f5a5         //   numCombinedSegments = numParametricEdges + numRadialEdges - 2 - 1
0004f5f4         //                       = numParametricSegments + 1 + numRadialSegments + 1 - 2 - 1
0004f651         //                       = numParametricSegments + numRadialSegments - 1
0004f6a2         //
0004f6ad         float numCombinedSegments = numParametricSegments + numRadialSegments - 1.0;
0004f703         if (P[0] == P[3] && tangents[0] == tangents[1]) {
0004f73d             // The vertex shader intentionally disabled our section. Set numCombinedSegments to 0.
0004f7a0             numCombinedSegments = 0.0;
0004f7c7         }
0004f7d2         // Pack the args for the evaluation stage.
0004f805         tcsPts01[gl_InvocationID] = vec4(P[0], P[1]);
0004f83b         tcsPt2Tan0[gl_InvocationID] = vec4(P[2], tangents[0]);
0004f87a         tcsTessArgs[gl_InvocationID] = vec3(numCombinedSegments, numParametricSegments,
0004f8d2                                             rotation / numRadialSegments);
0004f91d         if (gl_InvocationID == 2) {
0004f941             tcsEndPtEndTan = vec4(P[3], tangents[1]);
0004f977         }
0004f982         barrier();
0004f996         // Tessellate a quad strip with enough segments for the join plus all 3 curve sections
0004f9f5         // combined.
0004fa0a         float numTotalCombinedSegments = tcsJoinArgs0.x + tcsTessArgs[0].x + tcsTessArgs[1].x +
0004fa6a                                          tcsTessArgs[2].x;
0004faa6         if (tcsJoinArgs0.x != 0.0 && tcsJoinArgs0.x != numTotalCombinedSegments) {
0004faf9             // We are tessellating a quad strip with both a single-sided join and a double-sided
0004fb5a             // stroke. Add one more edge to the join. This new edge will fall parallel with the
0004fbba             // first edge of the stroke, eliminating artifacts on the transition from single
0004fc17             // sided to double.
0004fc37             ++tcsJoinArgs0.x;
0004fc55             ++numTotalCombinedSegments;
0004fc7d         }
0004fc88         numTotalCombinedSegments = min(numTotalCombinedSegments, MAX_TESSELLATION_SEGMENTS);
0004fce5         gl_TessLevelInner[0] = numTotalCombinedSegments;
0004fd1e         gl_TessLevelInner[1] = 2.0;
0004fd42         gl_TessLevelOuter[0] = 2.0;
0004fd66         gl_TessLevelOuter[1] = numTotalCombinedSegments;
0004fd9f         gl_TessLevelOuter[2] = 2.0;
0004fdc3         gl_TessLevelOuter[3] = numTotalCombinedSegments;
0004fdfc     }
0004fe03     float2 tangent, strokeCoord;
0004fe24     if (combinedEdgeID != 0 && !isFinalEdge) {
0004fe53         // Compute the location and tangent direction of the stroke edge with the integral id
0004feb1         // "combinedEdgeID", where combinedEdgeID is the sorted-order index of parametric and radial
0004ff16         // edges. Start by finding the tangent function's power basis coefficients. These define a
0004ff79         // tangent direction (scaled by some uniform value) as:
0004ffb9         //                                                 |T^2|
0004fffa         //     Tangent_Direction(T) = dx,dy = |A  2B  C| * |T  |
0005003b         //                                    |.   .  .|   |1  |
0005007c         float2 A, B, C = p1 - p0;
0005009e         float2 D = p3 - p0;
000500ba         if (w >= 0.0) {
000500d2             // P0..P2 represent a conic and P3==P2. The derivative of a conic has a cumbersome
00050131             // order-4 denominator. However, this isn't necessary if we are only interested in a
00050192             // vector in the same *direction* as a given tangent line. Since the denominator scales
000501f6             // dx and dy uniformly, we can throw it out completely after evaluating the derivative
00050259             // with the standard quotient rule. This leaves us with a simpler quadratic function
000502ba             // that we use to find a tangent.
000502e8             C *= w;
000502fc             B = .5*D - C;
00050316             A = (w - 1.0) * D;
00050335             p1 *= w;
0005034a         } else {
0005035b             float2 E = p2 - p1;
0005037b             B = E - C;
00050392             A = fma(float2(-3), E, D);
000503b9         }
000503c3         // FIXME(crbug.com/800804,skbug.com/11268): Consider normalizing the exponents in A,B,C at
00050426         // this point in order to prevent fp32 overflow.
00050460         // Now find the coefficients that give a tangent direction from a parametric edge ID:
000504be         //
000504c9         //                                                                 |parametricEdgeID^2|
00050529         //     Tangent_Direction(parametricEdgeID) = dx,dy = |A  B_  C_| * |parametricEdgeID  |
00050589         //                                                   |.   .   .|   |1                 |
000505e9         //
000505f4         float2 B_ = B * (numParametricSegments * 2.0);
0005062b         float2 C_ = C * (numParametricSegments * numParametricSegments);
00050675         // Run a binary search to determine the highest parametric edge that is located on or before
000506da         // the combinedEdgeID. A combined ID is determined by the sum of complete parametric and
0005073b         // radial segments behind it. i.e., find the highest parametric edge where:
0005078f         //
0005079a         //    parametricEdgeID + floor(numRadialSegmentsAtParametricT) <= combinedEdgeID
000507f3         //
000507fe         float lastParametricEdgeID = 0.0;
00050828         float maxParametricEdgeID = min(numParametricSegments - 1.0, combinedEdgeID);
0005087e         // FIXME(crbug.com/800804,skbug.com/11268): This normalize() can overflow.
000508d1         float2 tan0norm = normalize(tan0);
000508fc         float negAbsRadsPerSegment = -abs(radsPerSegment);
00050937         float maxRotation0 = (1.0 + combinedEdgeID) * abs(radsPerSegment);
00050982         for (int exp = %i - 1; exp >= 0; --exp) {
000509b4             // Test the parametric edge at lastParametricEdgeID + 2^exp.
000509fd             float testParametricID = lastParametricEdgeID + exp2(float(exp));
00050a4b             if (testParametricID <= maxParametricEdgeID) {
00050a86                 float2 testTan = fma(float2(testParametricID), A, B_);
00050acd                 testTan = fma(float2(testParametricID), testTan, C_);
00050b13                 float cosRotation = dot(normalize(testTan), tan0norm);
00050b5a                 float maxRotation = fma(testParametricID, negAbsRadsPerSegment, maxRotation0);
00050bb9                 maxRotation = min(maxRotation, PI);
00050bed                 // Is rotation <= maxRotation? (i.e., is the number of complete radial segments
00050c4d                 // behind testT, + testParametricID <= combinedEdgeID?)
00050c95                 if (cosRotation >= cos(maxRotation)) {
00050ccc                     // testParametricID is on or before the combinedEdgeID. Keep it!
00050d21                     lastParametricEdgeID = testParametricID;
00050d5e                 }
00050d70             }
00050d7e         }
00050d89         // Find the T value of the parametric edge at lastParametricEdgeID.
00050dd5         float parametricT = lastParametricEdgeID / numParametricSegments;
00050e20         // Now that we've identified the highest parametric edge on or before the
00050e72         // combinedEdgeID, the highest radial edge is easy:
00050eae         float lastRadialEdgeID = combinedEdgeID - lastParametricEdgeID;
00050ef7         // Find the angle of tan0, or the angle between tan0norm and the positive x axis.
00050f51         float angle0 = acos(clamp(tan0norm.x, -1.0, 1.0));
00050f8c         angle0 = tan0norm.y >= 0.0 ? angle0 : -angle0;
00050fc4         // Find the tangent vector on the edge at lastRadialEdgeID.
00051008         float radialAngle = fma(lastRadialEdgeID, radsPerSegment, angle0);
00051053         tangent = float2(cos(radialAngle), sin(radialAngle));
00051091         float2 norm = float2(-tangent.y, tangent.x);
000510c7         // Find the T value where the tangent is orthogonal to norm. This is a quadratic:
00051121         //
0005112c         //     dot(norm, Tangent_Direction(T)) == 0
00051160         //
0005116b         //                         |T^2|
00051194         //     norm * |A  2B  C| * |T  | == 0
000511c2         //            |.   .  .|   |1  |
000511eb         //
000511f6         float a=dot(norm,A), b_over_2=dot(norm,B), c=dot(norm,C);
00051238         float discr_over_4 = max(b_over_2*b_over_2 - a*c, 0.0);
00051278         float q = sqrt(discr_over_4);
0005129e         if (b_over_2 > 0.0) {
000512bc             q = -q;
000512d0         }
000512da         q -= b_over_2;
000512f2         // Roots are q/a and c/q. Since each curve section does not inflect or rotate more than 180
00051356         // degrees, there can only be one tangent orthogonal to "norm" inside 0..1. Pick the root
000513b8         // nearest .5.
000513cf         float _5qa = -.5*q*a;
000513ed         float2 root = (abs(fma(q,q,_5qa)) < abs(fma(a,c,_5qa))) ? float2(q,a) : float2(c,q);
0005144a         float radialT = (root.t != 0.0) ? root.s / root.t : 0.0;
0005148b         radialT = clamp(radialT, 0.0, 1.0);
000514b8         if (lastRadialEdgeID == 0.0) {
000514df             // The root finder above can become unstable when lastRadialEdgeID == 0 (e.g., if
0005153d             // there are roots at exatly 0 and 1 both). radialT should always == 0 in this case.
0005159e             radialT = 0.0;
000515b9         }
000515c4         // Now that we've identified the T values of the last parametric and radial edges, our final
00051629         // T value for combinedEdgeID is whichever is larger.
00051667         float T = max(parametricT, radialT);
00051695         // Evaluate the cubic at T. Use De Casteljau's for its accuracy and stability.
000516ec         float2 ab = unchecked_mix(p0, p1, T);
0005171a         float2 bc = unchecked_mix(p1, p2, T);
00051748         float2 cd = unchecked_mix(p2, p3, T);
00051776         float2 abc = unchecked_mix(ab, bc, T);
000517a5         float2 bcd = unchecked_mix(bc, cd, T);
000517d4         float2 abcd = unchecked_mix(abc, bcd, T);
00051807         // Evaluate the conic weight at T.
00051832         float u = unchecked_mix(1.0, w, T);
0005185e         float v = w + 1 - u;  // == mix(w, 1, T)
0005188f         float uv = unchecked_mix(u, v, T);
000518bb         // If we went with T=parametricT, then update the tangent. Otherwise leave it at the radial
0005191f         // tangent found previously. (In the event that parametricT == radialT, we keep the radial
00051982         // tangent.)
00051997         if (T != radialT) {
000519b3             tangent = (w >= 0.0) ? bc*u - ab*v : bcd - abc;
000519ef         }
000519fa         strokeCoord = (w >= 0.0) ? abc/uv : abcd;
00051a2c     } else {
00051a39         // Edges at the beginning and end of the strip use exact endpoints and tangents. This
00051a97         // ensures crack-free seaming between instances.
00051ad0         tangent = (combinedEdgeID == 0) ? tan0 : tan1;
00051b07         strokeCoord = (combinedEdgeID == 0) ? p0 : p3;
00051b3e     }
00051b45     // Find how many parametric segments this stroke requires.
00051b84     float numParametricSegments;
00051ba5     if (w < 0) {
00051bb6         if (p0 == p1 && p2 == p3) {
00051bda             numParametricSegments = 1; // a line
00051c0b         } else {
00051c1c             numParametricSegments = wangs_formula_cubic(PRECISION, p0, p1, p2, p3, AFFINE_MATRIX);
00051c7f         }
00051c89     } else {
00051c96         numParametricSegments = wangs_formula_conic(PRECISION,
00051cd5                                                     AFFINE_MATRIX * p0,
00051d1d                                                     AFFINE_MATRIX * p1,
00051d65                                                     AFFINE_MATRIX * p2, w);
00051db1     }
00051db8     // Returns the length squared of the largest forward difference from Wang's cubic formula.
00051e17     float wangs_formula_max_fdiff_pow2(float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float2 p3,
00051e6a                                        float2x2 matrix) {
00051ea4         float2 d0 = matrix * (fma(float2(-2), p1, p2) + p0);
00051ee1         float2 d1 = matrix * (fma(float2(-2), p2, p3) + p1);
00051f1e         return max(dot(d0,d0), dot(d1,d1));
00051f4a     }
00051f50     float wangs_formula_cubic(float _precision_, float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float2 p3,
00051fad                               float2x2 matrix) {
00051fde         float m = wangs_formula_max_fdiff_pow2(p0, p1, p2, p3, matrix);
00052026         return max(ceil(sqrt(%f * _precision_ * sqrt(m))), 1.0);
00052067     }
0005206d     float wangs_formula_cubic_log2(float _precision_, float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float2 p3,
000520cf                                    float2x2 matrix) {
00052105         float m = wangs_formula_max_fdiff_pow2(p0, p1, p2, p3, matrix);
0005214d         return ceil(log2(max(%f * _precision_ * _precision_ * m, 1.0)) * .25);
0005219c     }
000521a3     float wangs_formula_conic_pow2(float _precision_, float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float w) {
00052205         // Translate the bounding box center to the origin.
00052241         float2 C = (min(min(p0, p1), p2) + max(max(p0, p1), p2)) * 0.5;
00052289         p0 -= C;
0005229a         p1 -= C;
000522ab         p2 -= C;
000522bd         // Compute max length.
000522dc         float m = sqrt(max(max(dot(p0,p0), dot(p1,p1)), dot(p2,p2)));
00052323         // Compute forward differences.
0005234b         float2 dp = fma(float2(-2.0 * w), p1, p0) + p2;
00052383         float dw = abs(fma(-2.0, w, 2.0));
000523af         // Compute numerator and denominator for parametric step size of linearization. Here, the
00052411         // epsilon referenced from the cited paper is 1/precision.
00052454         float rp_minus_1 = max(0.0, fma(m, _precision_, -1.0));
00052494         float numer = length(dp) * _precision_ + rp_minus_1 * dw;
000524d6         float denom = 4 * min(w, 1.0);
000524fe         return numer/denom;
0005251a     }
00052520     float wangs_formula_conic(float _precision_, float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float w) {
0005257d         float n2 = wangs_formula_conic_pow2(_precision_, p0, p1, p2, w);
000525c6         return max(ceil(sqrt(n2)), 1.0);
000525ef     }
000525f5     float wangs_formula_conic_log2(float _precision_, float2 p0, float2 p1, float2 p2, float w) {
00052657         float n2 = wangs_formula_conic_pow2(_precision_, p0, p1, p2, w);
000526a0         return ceil(log2(max(n2, 1.0)) * .5);
000526ce     }
000526d5     // Find the starting and ending tangents.
00052703     float2 tan0 = ((p0 == p1) ? (p1 == p2) ? p3 : p2 : p1) - p0;
00052744     float2 tan1 = p3 - ((p3 == p2) ? (p2 == p1) ? p0 : p1 : p2);
00052785     if (tan0 == float2(0)) {
000527a2         // The stroke is a point. This special case tells us to draw a stroke-width circle as a
00052802         // 180 degree point stroke instead.
0005282e         tan0 = float2(1,0);
0005284a         tan1 = float2(-1,0);
00052867     }
0005286e     float cross2d(vec2 a, vec2 b) {
00052892         return determinant(mat2(a,b));
000528b9     }
000528c0     // Find which direction the curve turns.
000528ed     // NOTE: Since the curve is not allowed to inflect, we can just check F'(.5) x F''(.5).
00052949     // NOTE: F'(.5) x F''(.5) has the same sign as (P2 - P0) x (P3 - P1)
00052992     float turn = cross_length_2d(p2 - p0, p3 - p1);
000529c6     float combinedEdgeID = abs(edgeID) - numEdgesInJoin;
000529ff     if (combinedEdgeID < 0) {
00052a1d         tan1 = tan0;
00052a32         // Don't let tan0 become zero. The code as-is isn't built to handle that case. tan0=0
00052a90         // means the join is disabled, and to disable it with the existing code we can leave
00052aed         // tan0 equal to tan1.
00052b0c         if (lastControlPoint != p0) {
00052b32             tan0 = p0 - lastControlPoint;
00052b5c         }
00052b66         turn = cross_length_2d(tan0, tan1);
00052b92     }
00052b99     // Calculate the curve's starting angle and rotation.
00052bd3     float cosTheta = cosine_between_vectors(tan0, tan1);
00052c0c     float rotation = acos(cosTheta);
00052c31     if (turn < 0) {
00052c45         // Adjust sign of rotation to match the direction the curve turns.
00052c90         rotation = -rotation;
00052cae     }
00052cb5     float numRadialSegments;
00052cd2     float strokeOutset = sign(edgeID);
00052cf9     if (combinedEdgeID < 0) {
00052d17         // We belong to the preceding join. The first and final edges get duplicated, so we only
00052d78         // have "numEdgesInJoin - 2" segments.
00052da7         numRadialSegments = numEdgesInJoin - 2;
00052dd7         numParametricSegments = 1;  // Joins don't have parametric segments.
00052e24         p3 = p2 = p1 = p0;  // Colocate all points on the junction point.
00052e6e         // Shift combinedEdgeID to the range [-1, numRadialSegments]. This duplicates the first
00052ece         // edge and lands one edge at the very end of the join. (The duplicated final edge will
00052f2e         // actually come from the section of our strip that belongs to the stroke.)
00052f82         combinedEdgeID += numRadialSegments + 1;
00052fb3         // We normally restrict the join on one side of the junction, but if the tangents are
00053011         // nearly equivalent this could theoretically result in bad seaming and/or cracks on the
00053072         // side we don't put it on. If the tangents are nearly equivalent then we leave the join
000530d3         // double-sided.
000530ec         float sinEpsilon = 1e-2;  // ~= sin(180deg / 3000)
00053127         bool tangentsNearlyParallel =
0005314d                 (abs(turn) * inversesqrt(dot(tan0, tan0) * dot(tan1, tan1))) < sinEpsilon;
000531a8         if (!tangentsNearlyParallel || dot(tan0, tan1) < 0) {
000531e6             // There are two edges colocated at the beginning. Leave the first one double sided
00053246             // for seaming with the previous stroke. (The double sided edge at the end will
000532a2             // actually come from the section of our strip that belongs to the stroke.)
000532fa             if (combinedEdgeID >= 0) {
00053321                 strokeOutset = (turn < 0) ? min(strokeOutset, 0) : max(strokeOutset, 0);
0005337a             }
00053388         }
00053392         combinedEdgeID = max(combinedEdgeID, 0);
000533c3     } else {
000533d0         // We belong to the stroke.
000533f4         float maxCombinedSegments = NUM_TOTAL_EDGES - numEdgesInJoin - 1;
0005343e         numRadialSegments = max(ceil(abs(rotation) * NUM_RADIAL_SEGMENTS_PER_RADIAN), 1);
00053498         numRadialSegments = min(numRadialSegments, maxCombinedSegments);
000534e1         numParametricSegments = min(numParametricSegments,
0005351c                                     maxCombinedSegments - numRadialSegments + 1);
0005356e     }
00053575     // Additional parameters for emitTessellationCode().
000535ae     float radsPerSegment = rotation / numRadialSegments;
000535e7     float numCombinedSegments = numParametricSegments + numRadialSegments - 1;
00053636     bool isFinalEdge = (combinedEdgeID >= numCombinedSegments);
00053676     if (combinedEdgeID > numCombinedSegments) {
000536a6         strokeOutset = 0;  // The strip has more edges than we need. Drop this one.
000536fa     }
00053701     float2 p0=pts01Attr.xy, p1=pts01Attr.zw, p2=pts23Attr.xy, p3=pts23Attr.zw;
00053750     float2 lastControlPoint = argsAttr.xy;
0005377b     float w = -1;  // w<0 means the curve is an integral cubic.
000537bb     if (is_conic_curve()) {
000537d7         // Conics are 3 points, with the weight in p3.
0005380e         w = p3.x;
00053820         p3 = p2;  // Setting p3 equal to p2 works for the remaining rotational logic.
00053876     }
0005387d float3 safe_mix(float3 a, float3 b, float T, float one_minus_T) {
000538bf     return a*one_minus_T + b*T;
000538e1 float2 eval_rational_cubic(float4x3 P, float T) {
00053913     float one_minus_T = 1.0 - T;
00053934     float3 ab = safe_mix(P[0], P[1], T, one_minus_T);
0005396a     float3 bc = safe_mix(P[1], P[2], T, one_minus_T);
000539a0     float3 cd = safe_mix(P[2], P[3], T, one_minus_T);
000539d6     float3 abc = safe_mix(ab, bc, T, one_minus_T);

00064087         // Determine how many edges to give to the round join. We emit the first and final edges
000640e8         // of the join twice: once full width and once restricted to half width. This guarantees
00064149         // perfect seaming by matching the vertices from the join as well as from the strokes on
000641aa         // either side.
000641c2         float joinRads = acos(cosine_between_vectors(p0 - lastControlPoint, tan0));
00064216         float numRadialSegmentsInJoin = max(ceil(joinRads * NUM_RADIAL_SEGMENTS_PER_RADIAN), 1);
00064277         // +2 because we emit the beginning and ending edges twice (see above comment).
000642cf         float numEdgesInJoin = numRadialSegmentsInJoin + 2;
0006430b         // The stroke section needs at least two edges. Don't assign more to the join than
00064366         // "NUM_TOTAL_EDGES - 2".
00064388         numEdgesInJoin = min(numEdgesInJoin, NUM_TOTAL_EDGES - 2);
000643cb float fn = x_plus_1 * (x_plus_1 - 2);
000643f1 %s.zw = derivatives * (arccoord/radii * 2);
0006441d float3 %s = (%s * %s.xy1);
00064439     // Find the tangents. It's imperative that we compute these tangents from the original
00064494     // (pre-chopping) input points or else the seams might crack.
000644d6     float2 prevJoinTangent = P[0] - prevControlPoint;
0006450c     float2 tan0 = ((P[1] == P[0]) ? P[2] : P[1]) - P[0];
00064545     float2 tan1 = (P[3] == P[2] || isinf(P[3].y)) ? P[2] - P[1] : P[3] - P[2];
00064595     if (tan0 == float2(0)) {
000645b2         // [p0, p0, p0, p3] is a reserved pattern that means this patch is a "bowtie".
00064609         P[3] = P[0];  // Colocate all the points on the center of the bowtie.
00064657         // Use the final curve section to draw the bowtie. Since the points are colocated, this
000646b7         // curve will register as a line, which overrides innerTangents as [tan0, tan0]. That
00064715         // disables the first two sections of the curve because their tangents and points are all
00064777         // equal.
00064789         tan0 = prevJoinTangent;
000647a9         prevJoinTangent = float2(0);  // Disable the join section.
000647ec     }
000647f3     if (tan1 == float2(0)) {
00064810         // [p0, p3, p3, p3] is a reserved pattern that means this patch is a join only. Colocate all
00064875         // the curve's points to ensure it gets disabled by the tessellation stages.
000648ca         P[1] = P[2] = P[3] = P[0];
000648ed         // Since the points are colocated, this curve will register as a line, which overrides
0006494c         // innerTangents as [tan0, tan0]. Setting tan1=tan0 as well results in all tangents and all
000649b0         // points being equal, which disables every section of the curve.
000649fa         tan1 = tan0;
00064a0f     }
00064a16     // Calculate the number of segments to chop the join into.
00064a55     float cosTheta = cosine_between_vectors(prevJoinTangent, tan0);
00064a99     float joinRotation = (cosTheta == 1) ? 0 : acos(cosTheta);
00064ad8     if (cross_length_2d(prevJoinTangent, tan0) < 0) {
00064b0e         joinRotation = -joinRotation;
00064b34     }
00064b3a     float joinRadialSegments = abs(joinRotation) * NUM_RADIAL_SEGMENTS_PER_RADIAN;
00064b8d     float numSegmentsInJoin = (joinRadialSegments != 0 /*Is the join non-empty?*/ &&
00064be2                                JOIN_TYPE >= 0 /*Is the join not a round type?*/)
00064c33             ? sign(JOIN_TYPE) + 1  // Non-empty bevel joins have 1 segment and miters have 2.
00064c91             : ceil(joinRadialSegments);  // Otherwise round up the number of radial segments.
00064cf0     // Extends the middle join edge to the miter point.
00064d28     float innerJoinRadiusMultiplier = 1;
00064d51     if (JOIN_TYPE > 0 /*Is the join a miter type?*/) {
00064d88         innerJoinRadiusMultiplier = miter_extent(cosTheta, JOIN_TYPE/*miterLimit*/);
00064ddd     }
00064de4     // Clamps join geometry to the exterior side of the junction.
00064e26     float2 joinOutsetClamp = float2(-1, 1);
00064e52     if (joinRadialSegments > .1 /*Does the join rotate more than 1/10 of a segment?*/) {
00064eab         // Only clamp if the join angle is large enough to guarantee there won't be cracks on
00064f09         // the interior side of the junction.
00064f37         joinOutsetClamp = (joinRotation < 0) ? float2(-1, 0) : float2(0, 1);
00064f84     }
00064f8b     // Pack join args for the tessellation control stage.
00064fc5     vsJoinArgs0 = float4(numSegmentsInJoin, innerJoinRadiusMultiplier, prevJoinTangent);
0006501e     vsJoinArgs1 = float3(joinRotation / numSegmentsInJoin, joinOutsetClamp);
0006506c     // Now find where to chop the curve so the resulting sub-curves are convex and do not rotate
000650cd     // more than 180 degrees. We don't need to worry about cusps because the caller chops those out
00065131     // on the CPU. Start by finding the cubic's power basis coefficients. These define the bezier
00065193     // curve as:
000651a4     //
000651ab     //                                    |T^3|
000651db     //     Cubic(T) = x,y = |A  3B  3C| * |T^2| + P0
00065210     //                      |.   .   .|   |T  |
00065240     //
00065247     // And the tangent direction (scaled by a uniform 1/3) will be:
0006528b     //
00065292     //                                                 |T^2|
000652cf     //     Tangent_Direction(T) = dx,dy = |A  2B  C| * |T  |
0006530c     //                                    |.   .  .|   |1  |
00065349     //
00065350     float2 C = P[1] - P[0];
0006536c     float2 D = P[2] - P[1];
00065388     float2 E = P[3] - P[0];
000653a4     float2 B = D - C;
000653ba     float2 A = fma(float2(-3), D, E);
000653e1     // Now find the cubic's inflection function. There are inflections where F' x F'' == 0.
0006543d     // We formulate this as a quadratic equation:  F' x F'' == aT^2 + bT + c == 0.
00065490     // See: https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/research/wp-content/uploads/2005/01/p1000-loop.pdf
000654ef     // NOTE: We only need the roots, so a uniform scale factor does not affect the solution.
0006554c     float a = cross_length_2d(A, B);
00065571     float b = cross_length_2d(A, C);
00065596     float c = cross_length_2d(B, C);
000655bb     float b_over_2 = b*.5;
000655d6     float discr_over_4 = b_over_2*b_over_2 - a*c;
00065609     float2x2 innerTangents = float2x2(0);
00065633     if (discr_over_4 <= 0) {
00065650         // The curve does not inflect. This means it might rotate more than 180 degrees instead.
000656b1         // Craft a quadratic whose roots are the points were rotation == 180 deg and 0. (These are
00065714         // the points where the tangent is parallel to tan0.)
00065752         //
0006575d         //      Tangent_Direction(T) x tan0 == 0
0006578e         //      (AT^2 x tan0) + (2BT x tan0) + (C x tan0) == 0
000657cd         //      (A x C)T^2 + (2B x C)T + (C x C) == 0  [[because tan0 == P1 - P0 == C]]
00065825         //      bT^2 + 2cT + 0 == 0  [[because A x C == b, B x C == c]]
0006586d         //
00065878         // NOTE: When P0 == P1 then C != tan0, C == 0 and these roots will be undefined. But that's
000658dc         // ok because when P0 == P1 the curve cannot rotate more than 180 degrees anyway.
00065936         a = b;
00065945         b_over_2 = c;
0006595b         c = 0;
0006596a         discr_over_4 = b_over_2*b_over_2;
00065994         innerTangents[0] = -C;
000659b3     }
000659ba     // Solve our quadratic equation for the chop points. This is inspired by the quadratic formula
00065a1d     // from Numerical Recipes in C.
00065a41     float q = sqrt(discr_over_4);
00065a63     if (b_over_2 > 0) {
00065a7b         q = -q;
00065a8b     }
00065a91     q -= b_over_2;
00065aa4     float2 chopT = float2((a != 0) ? q/a : 0,
00065ad2                           (q != 0) ? c/q : 0);
00065b02     // Reposition any chop points that fall outside ~0..1 and clear their innerTangent.
00065b5a     int numOutside = 0;
00065b72     if (chopT[0] <= kParametricEpsilon || chopT[0] >= 1 - kParametricEpsilon) {
00065bc2         innerTangents[0] = float2(0);
00065be8         ++numOutside;
00065bfe     }
00065c04     if (chopT[1] <= kParametricEpsilon || chopT[1] >= 1 - kParametricEpsilon) {
00065c54         // Swap places with chopT[0]. This ensures chopT[0] is outside when numOutside > 0.
00065cb0         chopT = chopT.ts;
00065cca         innerTangents = float2x2(0,0, innerTangents[0]);
00065d03         ++numOutside;
00065d19     }
00065d1f     if (numOutside == 2) {
00065d3a         chopT[1] = 2/3.0;
00065d54     }
00065d5a     if (numOutside >= 1) {
00065d75         chopT[0] = (chopT[1] <= .5) ? chopT[1] * .5 : fma(chopT[1], .5, .5);
00065dc2     }
00065dc9     // Sort the chop points.
00065de6     if (chopT[0] > chopT[1]) {
00065e05         chopT = chopT.ts;
00065e1f         innerTangents = float2x2(innerTangents[1], innerTangents[0]);
00065e65     }
00065e6c     // If the curve is a straight line, point, or conic, don't chop it into sections after all.
00065ecc     if ((P[0] == P[1] && P[2] == P[3]) || isinf(P[3].y)) {
00065f07         chopT = float2(0);
00065f22         innerTangents = float2x2(tan0, tan0);
00065f50     }
00065f57     // Chop the curve at chopT[0] and chopT[1].
00065f87     float4 ab = unchecked_mix(P[0].xyxy, P[1].xyxy, chopT.sstt);
00065fc8     float4 bc = unchecked_mix(P[1].xyxy, P[2].xyxy, chopT.sstt);
00066009     float4 cd = isinf(P[3].y) ? P[2].xyxy : unchecked_mix(P[2].xyxy, P[3].xyxy, chopT.sstt);
00066066     float4 abc = unchecked_mix(ab, bc, chopT.sstt);
0006609a     float4 bcd = unchecked_mix(bc, cd, chopT.sstt);
000660ce     float4 abcd = unchecked_mix(abc, bcd, chopT.sstt);
00066105     float4 middle = unchecked_mix(abc, bcd, chopT.ttss);

0006e365         half4 main(float2 coord) {
0006e388             half t = half(coord.x);
0006e3ad             // Choose a chunk from thresholds via binary search in a loop.
0006e3f8             int low = 0;
0006e411             int high = %d;
0006e42c             int chunk = %d;
0006e448             for (int loop = 0; loop < %d; ++loop) {
0006e47c                 if (t < thresholds[chunk].w) {
0006e4ab                     high = chunk;
0006e4cd                 } else {
0006e4e6                     low = chunk + 1;
0006e50b                 }
0006e51d                 chunk = (low + high) / 2;
0006e547             }
0006e556             // Choose the final position via explicit 4-way binary search.
0006e5a1             int pos;
0006e5b6             if (t < thresholds[chunk].y) {
0006e5e1                 pos = (t < thresholds[chunk].x) ? 0 : 1;
0006e61a             } else {
0006e62f                 pos = (t < thresholds[chunk].z) ? 2 : 3;
0006e668             }
0006e676             @if (%d > 0) {
0006e691                 pos += 4 * chunk;
0006e6b3             }
0006e6c1             return t * scale[pos] + bias[pos];
0006e6f0         }

0006ec86                 } else {
0006ec9f                     // Simple repeat mode
0006ecc9                     t.x = fract(t.x);
0006ecef                 }
0006ed02                 // Always sample from (x, 0), discarding y, since the layout FP can use y as a
0006ed61                 // side-channel.
0006ed82                 half4 outColor = colorizer.eval(t.x0);
0006edb9                 if (bool(makePremul)) {
0006ede1                     outColor.rgb *= outColor.a;
0006ee11                 }
0006ee23                 return outColor;
0006ee44             }
0006ee52         }
0006ee5c     
0006ee61 const int kFillBW = 0;const int kFillAA = 1;const int kInverseFillBW = 2;const int kInverseFillAA = 3;
0006eec8         uniform int edgeType;  // GrClipEdgeType, specialized
0006ef06         // The circle uniform is (center.x, center.y, radius + 0.5, 1 / (radius + 0.5)) for regular
0006ef6a         // fills and (..., radius - 0.5, 1 / (radius - 0.5)) for inverse fills.
0006efba         uniform float4 circle;
0006efda         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 inColor) {
0006f009             // TODO: Right now the distance to circle calculation is performed in a space normalized
0006f06e             // to the radius and then denormalized. This is to mitigate overflow on devices that
0006f0cf             // don't have full float.
0006f0f5             half d;
0006f109             if (edgeType == kInverseFillBW || edgeType == kInverseFillAA) {
0006f155                 d = half((length((circle.xy - sk_FragCoord.xy) * circle.w) - 1.0) * circle.z);
0006f1b4             } else {
0006f1c9                 d = half((1.0 - length((circle.xy - sk_FragCoord.xy) *  circle.w)) * circle.z);
0006f229             }
0006f237             if (edgeType == kFillAA || edgeType == kInverseFillAA) {
0006f27c                 return inColor * saturate(d);
0006f2aa             } else {
0006f2bf                 return d > 0.5 ? inColor : half4(0);
0006f2f4             }
0006f302         }

0006f312         uniform half bias;

0006f381         half4 main(float2 coord) {
0006f3a4             half angle = bool(useAtanWorkaround)
0006f3d5                     ? half(2 * atan(-coord.y, length(coord) - coord.x))
0006f41d                     : half(atan(-coord.y, -coord.x));
0006f454             // 0.1591549430918 is 1/(2*pi), used since atan returns values [-pi, pi]
0006f4a9             half t = (angle * 0.1591549430918 + 0.5 + bias) * scale;
0006f4ee             return half4(t, 1, 0, 0); // y = 1 for always valid
0006f52e         }

0006f64c         uniform shader maskFP;
0006f66b         uniform half innerThreshold;
0006f690         uniform half outerThreshold;
0006f6b6         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 color) {
0006f6e3             half4 mask_color = maskFP.eval(xy);
0006f713             if (mask_color.a < 0.5) {
0006f739                 if (color.a > outerThreshold) {
0006f769                     half scale = outerThreshold / color.a;
0006f7a4                     color.rgb *= scale;
0006f7cc                     color.a = outerThreshold;
0006f7fa                 }
0006f80c             } else if (color.a < innerThreshold) {
0006f83f                 half scale = innerThreshold / max(0.001, color.a);
0006f882                 color.rgb *= scale;
0006f8a6                 color.a = innerThreshold;
0006f8d0             }
0006f8de             return color;
0006f8f8         }
0006f902     
0006f908         uniform half4x4 m;
0006f923         uniform half4   v;
0006f93e         uniform int unpremulInput;   // always specialized
0006f979         uniform int clampRGBOutput;  // always specialized
0006f9b4         uniform int premulOutput;    // always specialized
0006f9ef         half4 main(half4 color) {
0006fa11             if (bool(unpremulInput)) {
0006fa38                 color = unpremul(color);
0006fa61             }
0006fa6f             color = m * color + v;
0006fa92             if (bool(clampRGBOutput)) {
0006faba                 color = saturate(color);
0006fae3             } else {
0006faf8                 color.a = saturate(color.a);
0006fb25             }
0006fb33             if (bool(premulOutput)) {
0006fb59                 color.rgb *= color.a;
0006fb7f             }
0006fb8d             return color;
0006fba7         }
0006fbb1     
0006fbb7         half4 main(half4 color) {
0006fbd9             half3   hsl = color.rgb;
0006fbff             half      C = (1 - abs(2 * hsl.z - 1)) * hsl.y;
0006fc3b             half3     p = hsl.xxx + half3(0, 2/3.0, 1/3.0);
0006fc77             half3     q = saturate(abs(fract(p) * 6 - 3) - 1);
0006fcb6             half3   rgb = (q - 0.5) * C + hsl.z;
0006fce8             color = saturate(half4(rgb, color.a));
0006fd1b             color.rgb *= color.a;
0006fd3d             return color;
0006fd57         }
0006fd61     
0006fd67         half4 main(half4 halfColor) {
0006fd8d             float4 color = float4(halfColor);
0006fdbb             color = floor(color * 255 + 0.5) / 255;
0006fdef             color.rgb = color.a <= 0 ? half3(0) : floor(color.rgb / color.a * 255 + 0.5) / 255;
0006fe4f             return color;
0006fe69         }
0006fe73     
0006fe79         half4 main(half4 halfColor) {
0006fe9f             float4 color = float4(halfColor);
0006fecd             color = floor(color * 255 + 0.5) / 255;
0006ff01             color.rgb = floor(color.rgb * color.a * 255 + 0.5) / 255;
0006ff47             return color;
0006ff61         }

0006ff71         uniform shader srcFP;
0006ff8f         uniform shader dstFP;
0006ffad         uniform half4 k;
0006ffc6         uniform half pmClamp;
0006ffe4         half4 main(float2 xy) {
00070004             half4 src = srcFP.eval(xy);
0007002c             half4 dst = dstFP.eval(xy);
00070054             half4 color = saturate(k.x * src * dst +
00070089                                    k.y * src +
000700b8                                    k.z * dst +
000700e7                                    k.w);
00070110             color.rgb = min(color.rgb, max(color.a, pmClamp));
0007014f             return color;
00070169         }
00070173     
00070179         uniform shader colorizer;
0007019b         uniform shader gradLayout;
000701bf         uniform half4 leftBorderColor;  // t < 0.0
000701f2         uniform half4 rightBorderColor; // t > 1.0
00070226         uniform int makePremul;              // specialized
00070262         uniform int layoutPreservesOpacity;  // specialized
0007029f         half4 main(float2 coord) {
000702c2             half4 t = gradLayout.eval(coord);
000702f0             half4 outColor;
0007030d             // If t.x is below 0, use the left border color without invoking the child processor.
0007036f             // If any t.x is above 1, use the right border color. Otherwise, t is in the [0, 1]
000703cf             // range assumed by the colorizer FP, so delegate to the child processor.
00070425             if (!bool(layoutPreservesOpacity) && t.y < 0) {
00070461                 // layout has rejected this fragment (rely on sksl to remove this branch if the
000704c1                 // layout FP preserves opacity is false)
000704fa                 outColor = half4(0);
0007051f             } else if (t.x < 0) {
00070541                 outColor = leftBorderColor;
0007056d             } else if (t.x > 1.0) {
00070591                 outColor = rightBorderColor;
000705be             } else {
000705d3                 // Always sample from (x, 0), discarding y, since the layout FP can use y as a
00070632                 // side-channel.
00070653                 outColor = colorizer.eval(t.x0);
00070684             }
00070692             if (bool(makePremul)) {
000706b6                 outColor.rgb *= outColor.a;
000706e2             }
000706f0             return outColor;
0007070d         }
00070717     
0007071c const int kFillBW = 0;const int kFillAA = 1;const int kInverseFillBW = 2;const int kInverseFillAA = 3;
00070783         uniform int edgeType;  // GrClipEdgeType, specialized
000707c1         uniform float4 rectUniform;
000707e6         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 inColor) {
00070815             half coverage;
00070830             if (edgeType == kFillBW || edgeType == kInverseFillBW) {
00070875                 // non-AA
0007088f                 coverage = all(greaterThan(float4(sk_FragCoord.xy, rectUniform.zw),
000708e3                                            float4(rectUniform.xy, sk_FragCoord.xy))) ? 1 : 0;
00070941             } else {
00070956                 // compute coverage relative to left and right edges, add, then subtract 1 to
000709b4                 // account for double counting. And similar for top/bottom.
00070a00                 half4 dists4 = clamp(half4(1, 1, -1, -1) *
00070a3b                                      half4(sk_FragCoord.xyxy - rectUniform), 0, 1);
00070a8f                 half2 dists2 = dists4.xy + dists4.zw - 1;
00070ac9                 coverage = dists2.x * dists2.y;
00070af9             }
00070b08             if (edgeType == kInverseFillBW || edgeType == kInverseFillAA) {
00070b54                 coverage = 1.0 - coverage;
00070b7f             }
00070b8e             return inColor * coverage;
00070bb5         }
00070bbf     
00070bc5         // Effect that is a LUT for integral of normal distribution. The value at x:[0,6*sigma] is
00070c28         // the integral from -inf to (3*sigma - x). I.e. x is mapped from [0, 6*sigma] to
00070c82         // [3*sigma to -3*sigma]. The flip saves a reversal in the shader.
00070ccd         uniform shader integral;
00070cef         uniform float4 rect;
00070d0c         uniform int isFast;  // specialized
00070d39         half4 main(float2 pos, half4 inColor) {
00070d69             half xCoverage, yCoverage;
00070d90             if (bool(isFast)) {
00070db0                 // Get the smaller of the signed distance from the frag coord to the left and right
00070e14                 // edges and similar for y.
00070e40                 // The integral texture goes "backwards" (from 3*sigma to -3*sigma), So, the below
00070ea3                 // computations align the left edge of the integral texture with the inset rect's
00070f05                 // edge extending outward 6 * sigma from the inset rect.
00070f4e                 half2 xy = max(half2(rect.LT - pos), half2(pos - rect.RB));
00070f9a                 xCoverage = integral.eval(half2(xy.x, 0.5)).a;
00070fd9                 yCoverage = integral.eval(half2(xy.y, 0.5)).a;
00071018             } else {
0007102d                 // We just consider just the x direction here. In practice we compute x and y
0007108b                 // separately and multiply them together.
000710c5                 // We define our coord system so that the point at which we're evaluating a kernel
00071128                 // defined by the normal distribution (K) at 0. In this coord system let L be left
0007118b                 // edge and R be the right edge of the rectangle.
000711cd                 // We can calculate C by integrating K with the half infinite ranges outside the
0007122e                 // L to R range and subtracting from 1:
00071266                 //   C = 1 - <integral of K from from -inf to  L> - <integral of K from R to inf>
000712c8                 // K is symmetric about x=0 so:
000712f8                 //   C = 1 - <integral of K from from -inf to  L> - <integral of K from -inf to -R>
0007135d                 // The integral texture goes "backwards" (from 3*sigma to -3*sigma) which is
000713ba                 // factored in to the below calculations.
000713f4                 // Also, our rect uniform was pre-inset by 3 sigma from the actual rect being
00071452                 // blurred, also factored in.
00071480                 half4 rect = half4(half2(rect.LT - pos), half2(pos - rect.RB));
000714d0                 xCoverage = 1 - integral.eval(half2(rect.L, 0.5)).a
00071514                               - integral.eval(half2(rect.R, 0.5)).a;
00071559                 yCoverage = 1 - integral.eval(half2(rect.T, 0.5)).a
0007159d                               - integral.eval(half2(rect.B, 0.5)).a;
000715e2             }
000715f0             return inColor * xCoverage * yCoverage;
00071624         }
0007162e     
00071633 const int kFillBW = 0;const int kFillAA = 1;const int kInverseFillBW = 2;const int kInverseFillAA = 3;
0007169a         uniform int edgeType;      // GrClipEdgeType, specialized
000716dc         uniform int medPrecision;  // !sk_Caps.floatIs32Bits, specialized
00071727         uniform float4 ellipse;
00071747         uniform float2 scale;    // only for medPrecision
00071782         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 inColor) {
000717b1             // d is the offset to the ellipse center
000717e6             float2 d = sk_FragCoord.xy - ellipse.xy;
0007181b             // If we're on a device with a "real" mediump then we'll do the distance computation in
0007187f             // a space that is normalized by the larger radius or 128, whichever is smaller. The
000718e0             // scale uniform will be scale, 1/scale. The inverse squared radii uniform values are
00071942             // already in this normalized space. The center is not.
00071986             if (bool(medPrecision)) {
000719ac                 d *= scale.y;
000719ca             }
000719d8             float2 Z = d * ellipse.zw;
000719ff             // implicit is the evaluation of (x/rx)^2 + (y/ry)^2 - 1.
00071a45             float implicit = dot(Z, d) - 1;
00071a71             // grad_dot is the squared length of the gradient of the implicit.
00071ac0             float grad_dot = 4 * dot(Z, Z);
00071aec             // Avoid calling inversesqrt on zero.
00071b1e             if (bool(medPrecision)) {
00071b44                 grad_dot = max(grad_dot, 6.1036e-5);
00071b79             } else {
00071b8e                 grad_dot = max(grad_dot, 1.1755e-38);
00071bc4             }
00071bd2             float approx_dist = implicit * inversesqrt(grad_dot);
00071c14             if (bool(medPrecision)) {
00071c3a                 approx_dist *= scale.x;
00071c62             }
00071c71             half alpha;
00071c89             if (edgeType == kFillBW) {
00071cb0                 alpha = approx_dist > 0.0 ? 0.0 : 1.0;
00071ce7             } else if (edgeType == kFillAA) {
00071d15                 alpha = saturate(0.5 - half(approx_dist));
00071d50             } else if (edgeType == kInverseFillBW) {
00071d85                 alpha = approx_dist > 0.0 ? 1.0 : 0.0;
00071dbc             } else {  // edgeType == kInverseFillAA
00071df0                 alpha = saturate(0.5 + half(approx_dist));
00071e2b             }
00071e39             return inColor * alpha;
00071e5d         }
00071e67     
00071e6d         uniform colorFilter fp;
00071e8d         half4 main(half4 inColor) {
00071eb1             return fp.eval(inColor.rgb1) * inColor.a;
00071ee7         }
00071ef1     
00071ef7         uniform shader ninePatchFP;
00071f1c         uniform half cornerRadius;
00071f3f         uniform float4 proxyRect;
00071f61         uniform half blurRadius;
00071f83         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 inColor) {
00071fb2             // Warp the fragment position to the appropriate part of the 9-patch blur texture by
00072013             // snipping out the middle section of the proxy rect.
00072055             float2 translatedFragPosFloat = sk_FragCoord.xy - proxyRect.LT;
000720a1             float2 proxyCenter = (proxyRect.RB - proxyRect.LT) * 0.5;
000720e7             half edgeSize = 2.0 * blurRadius + cornerRadius + 0.5;
0007212b             // Position the fragment so that (0, 0) marks the center of the proxy rectangle.
00072188             // Negative coordinates are on the left/top side and positive numbers are on the
000721e5             // right/bottom.
00072202             translatedFragPosFloat -= proxyCenter;
00072236             // Temporarily strip off the fragment's sign. x/y are now strictly increasing as we
00072296             // move away from the center.
000722c0             half2 fragDirection = half2(sign(translatedFragPosFloat));
00072307             translatedFragPosFloat = abs(translatedFragPosFloat);
0007234a             // Our goal is to snip out the "middle section" of the proxy rect (everything but the
000723ac             // edge). We've repositioned our fragment position so that (0, 0) is the centerpoint
0007240d             // and x/y are always positive, so we can subtract here and interpret negative results
00072470             // as being within the middle section.
000724a3             half2 translatedFragPosHalf = half2(translatedFragPosFloat - (proxyCenter - edgeSize));
00072508             // Remove the middle section by clamping to zero.
00072546             translatedFragPosHalf = max(translatedFragPosHalf, 0);
0007258a             // Reapply the fragment's sign, so that negative coordinates once again mean left/top
000725ec             // side and positive means bottom/right side.
00072626             translatedFragPosHalf *= fragDirection;
0007265b             // Offset the fragment so that (0, 0) marks the upper-left again, instead of the center
000726bf             // point.
000726d5             translatedFragPosHalf += half2(edgeSize);
0007270c             half2 proxyDims = half2(2.0 * edgeSize);
00072741             half2 texCoord = translatedFragPosHalf / proxyDims;
00072782             return inColor * ninePatchFP.eval(texCoord).a;
000727bd         }
000727c7     
000727cd         uniform shader blurProfile;
000727f1         uniform half4 circleData;
00072814         half4 main(float2 xy, half4 inColor) {
00072843             // We just want to compute "(length(vec) - circleData.z + 0.5) * circleData.w" but need
000728a7             // to rearrange to avoid passing large values to length() that would overflow.
00072902             half2 vec = half2((sk_FragCoord.xy - circleData.xy) * circleData.w);
00072953             half dist = length(vec) + (0.5 - circleData.z) * circleData.w;
0007299e             return inColor * blurProfile.eval(half2(dist, 0.5)).a;
000729e1         }

000729f1         uniform colorFilter fp;  // Declared as colorFilter so we can pass a color

00072e2b         uniform half range;
00072e47         uniform shader table;

00072e92             half value = table.eval(sk_FragCoord.xy).a - 0.5; // undo the bias in the table
00072eee             // For each color channel, add the random offset to the channel value and then clamp
00072f4f             // between 0 and alpha to keep the color premultiplied.
00072f93             return half4(clamp(color.rgb + value * range, 0.0, color.a), color.a);
00072fe6         }
00072ff0     
00072ff6         half4 main(half4 c) {
00073014             half4 p = (c.g < c.b) ? half4(c.bg, -1,  2/3.0)
00073050                                   : half4(c.gb,  0, -1/3.0);
0007308d             half4 q = (c.r < p.x) ? half4(p.x, c.r, p.yw)
000730c7                                   : half4(c.r, p.x, p.yz);
00073103             // q.x  -> max channel value
0007312c             // q.yz -> 2nd/3rd channel values (unsorted)
00073165             // q.w  -> bias value dependent on max channel selection
000731ab             half eps = 0.0001;
000731ca             half pmV = q.x;
000731e6             half pmC = pmV - min(q.y, q.z);
00073212             half pmL = pmV - pmC * 0.5;
0007323a             half   H = abs(q.w + (q.y - q.z) / (pmC * 6 + eps));
0007327b             half   S = pmC / (c.a + eps - abs(pmL * 2 - c.a));
000732ba             half   L = pmL / (c.a + eps);
000732e5             return half4(H, S, L, c.a);
0007330d         }

00073441         uniform shader src;
0007345d         uniform float4 boundsUniform;
00073483         uniform float  xInvZoom;
000734a4         uniform float  yInvZoom;
000734c5         uniform float  xInvInset;
000734e7         uniform float  yInvInset;
00073509         uniform half2  offset;

0007354c             float2 zoom_coord = offset + coord * float2(xInvZoom, yInvZoom);
00073599             float2 delta = (coord - boundsUniform.xy) * boundsUniform.zw;
000735e3             delta = min(delta, float2(1.0) - delta);
00073618             delta *= float2(xInvInset, yInvInset);
0007364c             float weight = 0.0;
0007366c             if (delta.s < 2.0 && delta.t < 2.0) {
0007369e                 delta = float2(2.0) - delta;
000736cb                 float dist = length(delta);
000736f7                 dist = max(2.0 - dist, 0.0);
00073724                 weight = min(dist * dist, 1.0);
00073754             } else {
00073769                 float2 delta_squared = delta * delta;
0007379f                 weight = min(min(delta_squared.x, delta_squared.y), 1.0);
000737e9             }
000737f8             return src.eval(mix(coord, zoom_coord, weight));
00073835         }
